Spring and Autumn

Little Western Paradise 220

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 1 A Ghost Carries Distant Guests from Guanzhong, a Family With Nothing, and a Ferry Crossing Where People Lament the Qin Dynasty

Cheng Zhiqian thought that they were thanking him for taking them out for a trip, so he also repeatedly said that it was nothing. They were happy at the time, and they dispersed happily. Because Cheng Zhiqian had made an appointment to leave at 7:00 the next day, Zhang and Li got out of bed at 5:00 in the morning. According to their understanding, it was very early at this time. However, after they got out of bed, the people in the inn were already coming and going. Zhang and Li were shocked, fearing that they were late and Mr. Cheng had already left. They hurriedly walked to the outside of Zhiqian's window and looked inside, seeing him sleeping soundly on the bed, then they felt relieved. So the two of them waited quietly in the room. First, they heard Cheng Zhiqian wake up, then they heard him wash his face and drink tea, and then they heard a teahouse waiter leading someone in to report. After a while, he called out: "Mr. Zhang, Mr. Li, are you up yet? We can leave now. Director Wu didn't come, he just sent a car. Our car is going to be much more spacious." Li Shilian heard this and thought, "We've only been here for two days, and now we're going to visit the park and mausoleum? I'm not in the mood for that. To be honest, I'm completely here to meet Director Wu. Since he's not going, I don't want to go either." As he thought this, the words of excuse had not yet been spoken. Zhang Jiefu said: "Great, great, let's go." Shilian thought that since Jiefu had already agreed, he couldn't refuse either. Because Cheng Zhiqian and Director Wu were like brothers, and the chairman had invited him to dinner, it was always best not to offend him. So he reluctantly followed Zhang and Cheng into the car. When they came out of the gate, they found out that the Ministry of Education had sent a permanent secretary to accompany them, sitting in the car and not getting out. After Cheng Zhiqian's introduction, he finally met another person in the officialdom, and he felt a little more comforted. The car drove out of the West Gate and headed west along a very wide and flat road. (13)

Shorty Li 221

— Bai Ying

Shorty Li, from Tianjin, has been a guest in Hangzhou for a long time.

During the "January 28th" battle, he sent his military uniform photo from the Shanghai battlefield. He looked heroic and moving, but because of his short stature, he looked somewhat like a disguised Japanese person.

Attached to the photo was a short note. He said: "Our Chinese men must earn glory for our China!" He also said, "Hangzhou is not a place where our men should stay!" He called me to move to his hometown of Tianjin, or, like him, to join the army and go to the Shanghai battlefield.

Now he has sacrificed for our China, but how can we still remember that there was a Shorty Li who sacrificed for us!

The image of Shorty Li often swirls in my mind. Usually, he always bared his chest and said, "There are many stories in our Tianjin!" Once, he told us the origin of the big scar on his face: At that time, he was still in Tianjin, he beat a notorious Tianjin thug who was working for the Japanese. He was also hit with a stone by that thug, leaving a big hole and a lot of blood flowing from his head, but he didn't groan in pain.

His life history: He had sold art in the north for six years, opened a steamed bun shop in Suzhou, and lived in Hangzhou for three years.

He could also read, keep accounts, and hum a few poems. It is said that he had gone to school when he was young, and he was always proud of this. He often called himself a man of letters!

Alas! Shorty Li is dead! I can't think of any words to describe the longing in my heart, I can only imitate the tone of a lover and say: "Where has my beloved gone! ... Leaving only a photo that makes people cry!"

I often feel ashamed looking at the crooked words in that short note: "We are Chinese men!"

Tidbits 222

— (Xin Quan)

A certain county magistrate inspected the disaster situation in Xiang Township. The township head pawned clothes and slaughtered chickens and ducks to entertain him. During the banquet, the township head pleaded, "County Magistrate, please help us and send relief early, we are really suffering." The county magistrate said drunkenly, "What are you suffering! The people in our county are suffering even more than you. You have chicken and duck to eat in the countryside. I wish I could live in your countryside for the rest of my life."

Holiday Homework 223

— Shi Jihong

After a summer vacation of more than two months, Miss So-and-so passed the junior high school graduation exam this year. With nothing on her mind, she can enjoy herself. She got out of bed at nine thirteen in the morning, humming the tune of "Peanuts".

Before washing her face, she must first enjoy the cool breeze, standing on the balcony of the three-story building, it is already so hot in the morning.

Breakfast is placed on the table, usually untouched. She counts twenty-four copper coins and asks the maid to buy a bowl of eel noodles. While eating noodles, she reads the newspaper: supplement, local news, advertisements. Newspaper finished, noodles eaten.

Sitting in the living room is too boring, moving around will lose four ounces of meat. Holding a volume of picture stories for little brothers or sisters, children's picture newspaper, leaning on the rattan armchair, putting her feet up, shaking the banana leaf fan, although it is not as good as Lushan Qingdao, but carefree, happy, without a drop of sweat on her body. Tea comes when she wants it, and if it gets hotter, the electric fan turns on by itself. She sits until half past eleven, then strolls around for a while, and then she can have lunch.

After lunch, chatting and laughing, eating watermelon. Before long, it's already half past two, take a nap, better than swimming in the pool. She really doesn't know how to swim.

Weary eyes, she asks the maid to draw water for a bath, washing and washing every day, washing clean, sprinkling Three Flowers brand talcum powder to enjoy the cool breeze. She eats some snacks. Zhang's older sister sends a letter, "Come play mahjong tomorrow." Reading the evening newspaper, time flies so fast, the sky is dark again. It's good to run around outside, anyway, it's very cool, or hide around the house, muttering, "Why hasn't the report card come yet? The Education Bureau is really a mess." "The books for the second half of the year are really difficult!" "A horse-eye gem set in a ring costs only fifteen yuan."

Someone downstairs calls for dinner.

Stomach full, shaking the fan, enjoying the cool breeze, waiting until nine fifteen, going to bed and sleeping until dawn.

Another Weapon 224

— Shi Ying

Umbrella 225

— Ning Yi

When the sky leaks, except for those who have raincoats or automobiles, they always have to rely on this circular umbrella; it is also called a rain umbrella, as the name suggests, it seems to be used only for covering rain and not for other purposes! But there are exceptions. Women who catch dental worms on the street, regardless of whether it is sunny or rainy, are always hand-in-hand with it, forming an inextricable bond? As for farmers walking on the banks of fields, they often rely on it to resist the scorching sun, but people in the city, except when it rains, always disdain it. The umbrella repairer appears on rainy days, perhaps for this reason?

It is said that women's thighs can be bare, but their faces cannot withstand the sun? So when summer arrives, it becomes popular! In the street, it is often next to the ladies, but in fact, it is also because it dresses too beautifully in summer, unlike the usual brown cloth robe, it is not easy to be favored. As for the ladies? It is not entirely for sun protection, half is for decoration, because the newspaper often has the backs of women holding umbrellas [art photos] published, so one is used as a decoration, and the other is used to show off, mutually beneficial, and complement each other.

Because it is cumbersome to carry, men despise it very much, even if it rains, they do not bother to borrow it, but sometimes in order to please his beloved, they will shake hands with it?

Let's talk about this again, men are not absolutely incompatible with it, many of them like "flying umbrellas"! Isn't this clear evidence? A former classmate recently got a "flying umbrella". I said, "Old brother, you don't have to worry about rainy days?" He said, "This is for rain?"

Records of Ephemeral Incense 226

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of Qing, translated by Qin Shouou

Because all their money was truly too little, even the rice needed for the living was not enough. How could they then prepare the wine and dishes for the dead and the paper ingots for them to use? Thus, every year during the Qingming Festival, though they still went to sweep the graves, they absolutely did not bring wine, dishes, or paper ingots. They would simply dig up a few clumps of earth near the graves, personally carry them, and pile them on top of each grave. Then, from the willow trees by the roadside, they would casually break off a few tender green new willow branches and insert them in the center of the clumps of earth. 丨丨Because willow trees are the first to grow leaves each spring, people inevitably view them with favor.丨丨 As a kind of adornment. This kind of adornment was certainly not for passersby to admire; their intention was to let their ancestors know that although they were very poor, even unable to afford paper ingots, they still constantly remembered their ancestors in their hearts! In this way, although the ancestors did not have delicious wine and dishes to eat, nor paper money to use, they finally received a kind of comfort in their spirits. For the descendants to be able to make their ancestors' spirits in heaven comforted was, after all, a kind of "unceasing filial piety"! The last kind of people could not even prepare soil and new willows. The inability to prepare them, as mentioned here, certainly does not mean that they could not afford to buy soil or new willows, because these two things originally did not need money to buy. But perhaps their ancestral graves were too far from their homes. Either due to a lack of travel expenses or being too busy working to make a living, they could not go. There was no way but to let their ancestors suffer some grievance! Now, it is this desolate and lonely phenomenon displayed by this pile of communal graves that no one ever comes to sweep that has touched the Empress Dowager's heart, causing her to suddenly feel an indescribable sorrow during her extremely exciting journey. (122)

Small Records of Local Customs

A Few Small Impressions of Traveling North 227

— Yan Qiao

Although this time I only went as far as Tai'an, I have already stepped into the territory of the Northern Country. The customs of the Northern Country are naturally different from those of the Southern Country. There are a few small impressions that I will never forget.

Spring Couplets 丨 Whether in the city or outside the city, there is not a single household that does not paste a pair of spring couplets on its lintel. Added to this are four-character plaques. The sentences of the spring couplets are mostly auspicious words with a praising meaning, probably all ready-made sentences. However, the formerly commonly used "Imperial grace is as vast as spring, the literary governance shines like the sun" is now gone. In Qufu, there are often matters related to Confucius, indicating that they live in the land of the sage, and every family is nurtured by Confucianism, forming a seed of Confucian scholars. It is rare to see good calligraphy. This kind of non-popular art has become popular. There, the walls are all made of mud, with at most a few feet of bricks laid at the base. The architecture is so simple, yet they are unwilling to omit the spring couplets. Spring couplets, like the rouge of Southern Country girls, have become an indispensable decoration.

Rickshaws 丨 This is a sharp tool for cultural exchange. If there are rickshaws in this place, then new material civilization will gradually be transported over. Rickshaws originated in Japan, and Shanghai was the earliest to accept them. However, now, the rickshaws in Shanghai are far inferior to those in the Northern Country. They all have black bodies, so they really shouldn't be called "yellow package cars." Loudspeakers emit grand sounds, and white cloth awnings are installed above, providing shade for the pullers. The handles are inlaid with brass, some of which are polished brightly. The lights are also very grandly placed on the left and right, almost like the private cars in Shanghai. Unlike the yellow package cars in Suzhou, which are small and broken, when the awning is raised on a rainy day, your head will hit the top and your knees will hit the front, guaranteeing that you'll be as wet as a drowned chicken.

Flies 丨 In the Southern Country, people with even a little bit of hygiene knowledge hate flies like anything, but in the Northern Country, they are commonplace. Those items placed on open-air stalls are completely covered with flies, and no one drives them away. In these few days, watermelon rinds, peach and pear skins are all things that attract flies, so there is a constant buzzing sound everywhere. When we saw it, we didn't dare to buy anything. The vendors at the station are relatively more aware, and they know to cover the fruit with a very dense net, and the chicken cages have lids.

Toilets 丨 The toilets in the Northern Country are the dirtiest. The same goes for hotels. Only the "guesthouses" at a few major stations along the railway have flush toilets. If you want to solve the problem of excretion, you must first be proficient in the skill of climbing into the pit. Northern Country friends simply don't know how to use toilets, so the Yanzhou Railway Guesthouse has a flush toilet, which is considered a new invention adapted to local conditions.

Cloth 丨 It is rare to see people wearing silk clothes in the Northern Country. Most people use cloth. Even young girls wear cloth clothes, because they have not yet been contaminated by the Shanghai style. They do not have the courage to use gorgeous colors and fragrant scents to lure the opposite sex and make them pursue them. Therefore, I saw several female students, some wearing moon-white bamboo cloth, some wearing purple-background black-flower cloth, which is still the 19th century in the Southern Country. Men work even harder to use cloth, and it is rare to use silk for shoes. Moreover, the two primary colors of blue and white are the most commonly seen, which is the spirit of the Northern Country.

Once you cross the Yangtze River, everything changes. Could it be that the drought and the production of Southern Country friends are stronger than those of the Northern Country? I don't believe it!

Financial Speculation Initiates Gold Price Rebound of $2.90 228

▲ British Silver Recedes, Bullish ▲

The gold market was strong again yesterday. Major speculators covered their short positions, and market sentiment was excellent. The price once rose above the $50 mark. The market situation was still mediocre for half the day, and fluctuations were small. Early in the morning, overseas silver markets saw British silver recede and American silver remain flat. London raw gold fell by eight and a half pence. Although exchange rates rose, they were not affected. American cotton fell by seventeen pounds, and American wheat saw mixed ups and downs. Market sentiment was firm due to the major bank's clearing of silver accounts at the close of the previous day, the satisfaction of buyers, and the rumor that the United States had not purchased gold. The price of goods opened and immediately rose to $48. Trading preparations by gold merchants also showed a flat trend, but because the exchange market was ordinary and banks were still offering gold, the price briefly fell after the opening. However, market sentiment was very stable. Knowing that HSBC's listed exchange rates for British and American silver had each decreased by 0.125, and that the Central Bank also opened for cash transactions, the price rose after falling, but banks were still supplying gold. At this time, sellers were still eager, and the situation was not yet very bullish. However, under the relentless covering by Sen Changyong, the price was maintained with great effort. Chinese merchants also formed a union, and the exchange market gradually showed tightness, resulting in a situation of demand exceeding supply in the market. Major speculators such as Sen Changyong, Dadecheng, and Fuyu frantically purchased gold, and the gold price gradually rose and became firmer. Although there was a slow phase in the middle, the first-order prices had already tightened to the 5-pence mark, the buying interest was enthusiastic, and market sentiment was prosperous, so the price broke through the $50 mark. However, Yifeng, Yongfuxingyong, and Huixiang took advantage of the high price to sell off, and the midday close still succumbed to below the $50 mark. US Cotton Exports Decrease, Prices Increase 241

According to a report from the Textile Division of the U.S. Bureau of Foreign and Domestic Commerce, U.S. cotton exports in May totaled 285,000 bales, valued at $17,298,000. In May of last year, exports totaled 592,000 bales, valued at $25,787,000. U.S. cotton exports in May this year decreased by 102,000 bales, or 26%, compared to April of the same year. Over the past ten months, from August of last year to May of this year, U.S. cotton exports totaled 6,769,000 bales, valued at $370,307,600. This represents a decrease of 344,000 bales, or 5%, compared to the same period in the previous cotton season, but an increase in value of $95,831,000, or 35%.

Grains, Flour Futures Rise and Fall Irregularly 242

Results Present a Mixed Picture

The flour market fluctuated significantly. After the morning opening, all months followed the previous day's sharp decline, and dealers across the board sold back their holdings. The market was even more sluggish around noon, with near-month contracts down by about 0.04 yuan and far-month contracts down by more than 0.03 yuan. Market sentiment remained weak, as factories sought to hedge their positions due to sluggish actual sales. Dealers, aware of the weak factory demand and slow customer sales, also rushed to sell. This renewed downward pressure occurred due to both factories and dealers competing to sell. However, after the price decline, factories stopped selling. Speculators took advantage of the low prices to cover their short positions, attracting new long positions from both inside and outside the industry. Prices gradually rose, recovering by 0.04, 0.05, or 0.06 yuan. The spot market sales remained weak, down by a little over 0.01 yuan. July contracts are down 0.01 yuan each, November is up by a significant 0.05 yuan, and December and February are each up by 0.015 yuan.

The wheat market fluctuated. After the morning opening, foreign wheat rose slightly, and factory demand for spot wheat revived, triggering short covering. Contracts for all months rose across the board, especially near-month contracts due to short covering, with prices rising significantly by 0.04, 0.05, or 0.06 yuan. However, after the price increase, the flour market declined, and sentiment weakened again. Traders, seeing the futures prices rise, thought it more favorable to sell futures and buy spot. Selling pressure increased, and prices fell again in the afternoon, declining by 0.05, 0.06, or 0.07 yuan. At the close, the current month was still up by a significant 0.01 yuan, October and November were down by 0.01 yuan each, December was down by 0.02 yuan, January was down by 0.03 yuan, and February was down significantly by 0.06 yuan. After factories lowered prices, spot wheat opened yesterday at 35,000 bags. High-quality wheat from Shandong and other regions was discounted by 2.6 yuan, down 0.15 yuan from the previous week.

Silk and Tea: New York Stock Exchange to Auction Chinese Silk 249

The New York Raw Silk Exchange has only auctioned Japanese silk in the past. Chinese silk was auctioned for the first time on the 4th of this month, with factory silk of 20-22 denier and 83 points of uniformity as the auction standard. This is good news amidst the declining sales of Chinese silk in the United States. However, the labor unrest in the American textile industry is becoming more serious, making it difficult for silk sales to recover. Silk factories in Lyon and other places are also experiencing weak demand for raw silk due to sluggish silk fabric sales. Silk telegrams have not shown any signs of improvement, and market sentiment remains sluggish. Only silk merchants continue to purchase 20 packages of white factory silk and 5 packages of printed silk, and the price remains firm.

Page 20

Free Talk

"Minority" and "Special" 251

— Zhi Li

Mr. Liu Linsheng has written a book called "Parallel Prose," published by the Commercial Press. He also published an article titled "The Study Method of Parallel Prose" in the Commercial Press's "Publication Weekly." According to him, even in "this era of advocating literary reform," parallel prose, that "piled-up aristocratic literature," is still worth "studying" and learning to do. His reasons are as follows:

"Literature appreciated by a (minority) of people is called aristocratic literature by scholars. Assuming that this term is absolutely correct and unchangeable, then we must recognize two points: (1) Something supported by a (minority) of people is not necessarily bad. This has been the subject of heated discussion in political science. Expressing the opinions of minorities (minority representation) is a strategy in politics, so let's not go into detail. When it comes to literature, isn't it the same? Compared with poetry, there are always fewer people who appreciate Parallel Prose. (2) What is appreciated by a minority often becomes what is appreciated by a majority. Parallel prose may not have this trend, but the branches and remnants of Parallel Prose, such as congratulatory couplets, elegiac couplets, and hanging couplets, can indeed give people a lot to appreciate."

Another reason is that "Parallel Prose is a (special) product of our country" and is enough to "hold its head high" against Western literature.

Saying that things of "minority" people are good and that "special" things are valuable are not reasons that Mr. Liu found temporarily to defend Parallel Prose, but are fundamentally based on their ideology. I will use Mr. Liu's views on Parallel Prose to prove this point.

In Mr. Liu's "Parallel Prose Literature," he introduces many Parallel Prose writers, and the part about the Qing Dynasty is also published in "Publication Weekly." After the biography of each writer, he extracts the writer's aphorisms and includes comments, in the following format.

"Mao Qiling, style name Dake, from Xiaoshan. Scholars call him Mr. Xihe. A student of the Ming Dynasty. After the fall of the Ming Dynasty, he shaved his head and lived in the mountains, studying in an earthen room. During the Kangxi period, he was summoned for the Hongbo examination, awarded the position of reviewer, and compiled the History of the Ming Dynasty. Later, he asked to return home due to illness. He died at the age of ninety-four. His collected works on classics and literature total two hundred and thirty-four volumes.

Aphorisms: Since ancient times, when Jianwu achieved governance, he favored treacherous soldiers; when Zhenguan achieved peace, he indulged rebellious commands. (Ode to Ping滇) When the Zhu Banner wipes away tears, it all becomes rouge; when the plain axe loses its heart, do not govern the country. (Epitaph of Shen Yunying)

Xihe was a classicist who wrote literature, which was profound and did not fall into the fashion of the time. The epitaph of Shen Yunying is the most representative. Qian Jibo said that his writing was both regular and free, and not thorny."

Parallel Prose itself and the Parallel Prose of the Qing Dynasty have their own value. Looking at them as antiques has a different meaning, but if you want to see them, you must see the whole article. It is meaningless to extract one or two aphorisms to appreciate. (I have an article on "Aphorisms" discussing this in detail, so I won't talk about the principles here.) For example, Mao Xihe's aphorisms quoted above are indeed excellent in the original text, but they must be connected to the whole text to make sense. Now, if we look at them in isolation, what good can we see? Let's look at other aphorisms, and it's the same, such as Chen Qinian's "If a noble carriage enters Wei, fortunately mention Zhu Hai in the city; as for the purple ribbons touring Wu, I wish to describe Bo Luan in the hall." Yuan Zicai's "Like the sun watering frost and snow, everything it passes disappears; like a long drought getting clouds and rain, I'm afraid it will be too late to return."

However, why do some people only read aphorisms when they read articles? This is because of their ideology, because their ideology is individualistic, so their scope is narrow. In their minds, everything in the universe has no connection, but is a series of isolated things. Among the isolated phenomena, they find a phenomenon that is beneficial to themselves and worship it, regarding it as the representative and ruler of all phenomena. Therefore, in the eyes of these people, there is no whole universe, only a sun suspended in the sky; there is no whole nation-state, only emperors and generals; there is no history of connection and evolution, only (special) signs of prosperity and decline; and even when looking at flowers, they only look at a branch inserted in a vase, and when reading articles, they only look at a few sentences circled on the side...

All such people must value the (special), and will not recognize the essence of the universe or the structure of society at all. They will never understand the spirit of the masses.

Confucius (Continued) 252

— Cao Juren

(II)

"It's really unlucky. I'm starving, but I'm still so cheerfully poor. That bookworm!"

As soon as Zilu said "bookworm," he quickly covered his mouth with his hand, fearing that Zhongni would hear him.

"Zhong You, what are you saying?"

"Nothing. I said: Scholars serve the ruler and follow the Way, and get promoted and rich. Other people are so happy, but you, old Master, are unlucky all your life!"

"Oh! Those who truly have knowledge have no reason not to be poor!"

"Then there must be some shortcomings in their knowledge! Or we say "benevolence" and "love," but other people don't believe us. Or we are waiting for opportunities, but we have not seized them!"

"That's nonsense! Didn't Boyi and Shuqi starve to death? Why didn't Prince Bigan speculate well and wait for people to cut open his stomach? Alas! "Not a rhinoceros, not a tiger, wandering in the wilderness!" Why are we so unlucky!"

Zilu silently retreated, and Zigong walked in.

"Ci! You say: "Not a rhinoceros, not a tiger, wandering in the wilderness!" Why are we so unlucky?"

"Master must also compromise a bit! This society, this group of people, will always fail if they don't compromise."

"How can I compromise? "Am I a bitter gourd? How can I be tied up and not eat?" In the State of Lu, in the State of Chu, as long as there is an opportunity, I always seriously want to do something for them, but they always kick me away and let me roll around. Last time, even when Gongshan Buniu greeted me, I wanted to try it. Compromise, compromise, there is always a limit. How can you ask me to compromise?"

Zigong thought for a while and felt that he had nothing to say, so he retreated. Yan Yuan finally went in, and Zhongni said to him very warmly:

"Hui, you say: "Not a rhinoceros, not a tiger, wandering in the wilderness!" Why are we so unlucky?"

"Master, you don't have to think about these things. We have treasures, but they don't know the value of them, which shows that they are big fools. Why do we have to think about whether we are unlucky or not!"

Zhongni was so happy when he heard this that he jumped up and said:

"Okay, Hui! You be the boss, and I'll be the partner!"

× × × ×

"Phoenix, phoenix, what virtue has declined! The past cannot be advised, but the future can still be pursued?

Enough, enough, those who are in politics today are in danger!"

This long and mournful Chu song pierced Zhongni's heart! (End)

A Street I Commemorate 253

— Di Zhou

Walking on R Road plunged me into memories. I carefully gazed at a Western-style house by the roadside, its walls still red, but somewhat dim. It used to be a rectangular building behind the girls' dormitory and library, quiet and deserted. Right there, the stove was burning inside, the small space filled with people reading, each with passion burning faintly in their mind; each with expectations shimmering indistinctly in their heart. Naturally, each was their own person, but they also had things in common.

Walking a few more steps slowly, the left side of the building, with many windows, faced me. The windows are now tightly closed. Open them and let the sunlight into the classroom! Yes, it was late winter and early spring then, the icy cold air assaulting us even in the daytime. We opened all the windows, letting the cold air and sunlight in. We concentrated on moving our pencils, recording the lecturer's notes in our notebooks. What admiring, joyful, and determined gazes shone from my eyes! At night, the lights were bright, like a grand banquet in full swing, hearts pounding, faces flushed, ascending the podium, "Students, where is the driving force of social evolution? Tonight we will answer this question..." The resounding voice tensed the air. The night lost its silence, resembling the ebb and flow of the tide, covered by the 'sizzling' sound of the rushing wind. Late at night, everyone was still excited, patting each other on the shoulders, striding out of the school gate...

A little further away, the lawn lay in the sunlight, unchanged, except that the grass then seemed greener, and people holding books scattered around, walking or standing still. In the early morning and at dusk, many people would gather around, like in a club, laughing loudly and talking loudly. Or two or three would walk and talk. I also spoke in a low voice with someone:

"This is no ordinary school! From all over the towns and villages, our classmates have returned from there, wanting to gain profound knowledge."

"Those who have returned from the front lines of life are indeed different. I studied for seven years in the past, but it's not comparable to one day of classes here."

Facing the lawn was the open reading room. Although I can't see it now, the impression is as clear as the scene before my eyes. Every morning, before the newspaper delivery, people were already waiting there quietly. The newspaper was always held down by this hand or that hand, and I often waited, the time extending silently, still crowded, so I focused on the posture of the newspaper readers. Most of them were thinking as they read, one question after another, revealing a passionate half-profile. Impatient, I would squeeze in and read with them.

Leaving the reading room, small groups of two or three walked towards the lawn, talking softly. Originally, I had only a vague understanding of international politics, but in this atmosphere of several months, I began to have a clearer understanding. I began to understand to take notes on major domestic and international events in a small notebook.

R Road, a street I commemorate.

Walking more than a mile west from the red Western-style house, there is a north-facing house, in which there is a room, and I occupied a space with a bed. Riazanov's popular English translation, I was there leaning against the wide window, reading a section, then looking out over the square open space, my gaze resting on a corner of the distant sky. There, I had intense friendships, and we often talked until late at night. I remember one evening, I wrote the following lines of poetry:

"I have no other thoughts, I am only immersed in learning and friendship."

"Quiet life is leaping, like a swift wind sweeping across the autumn sky."

R Road, a street I commemorate. I couldn't help but walk back the way I came, heading east. Unfortunately, it wasn't quitting time, otherwise, I would have seen thousands upon thousands of workers, becoming a flood, overflowing in all directions. And I would have heard the banter of male and female workers, dissolving their fatigue of the day. I reached the eastern end of R Road, the filthy river, unchanging year after year, as if it were a reservoir of sweat full of dust and coal smoke from the workers' bodies. The factory buildings still stood tall and solemn, the sound of machines still ringing and roaring, but standing by the river, I no longer felt filled with the romantic revolutionary fervor that could be sung and wept.

That was five years ago. Walking on R Road, I thought of the past, which stands at the crossroads in my memory.

Literary Talk Outside the Door 254

— Hua Yu

(10) No Need to Panic

Last time I said that among the illiterate masses, there have always been writers. I haven't been to the countryside for a long time. Previously, when farmers had some free time, such as when cooling off, someone would tell stories. However, these storytellers were usually specific people who had relatively more knowledge and were good at speaking, able to make people listen, understand, and find it interesting. This is the writer, and copying down his words is the work. If someone's language is uninteresting and they are overly talkative, people won't listen and will give them cold remarks—satire. We have been using literary Chinese for thousands of years and vernacular Chinese for over a decade. Everyone who can write is not necessarily a literary figure, right? Even if they all became literary figures, they are not warlords or bandits, so they would not harm the masses, but just read each other's works.

There is also a fear of the decline of literature. The masses do not have the cultivation of old literature, and compared to the refinement of the literature of the literati, it may appear to be "declining." But it is not infected with the chronic diseases of old literature, so it is vigorous and fresh. Anonymous literature such as "Midnight Song" will give old literature a new strength, as I said before; now some people have also introduced many folk songs and stories. There is also drama, such as the "Self-Biography of the Impermanence Ghost" cited in "Picking Flowers at Dawn" from "Mulian Saves His Mother," which says that because he sympathized with a ghost, he temporarily released him back to the world for half a day, but was punished by Yama and never dared to be lenient again.

"I fear neither copper walls nor iron walls!

I fear neither imperial relatives nor nobles!"

How humane, how knowledgeable, how law-abiding, and how decisive! Can our literary figures do this?

This is a true work of farmers and manual laborers, occasionally performed by them, using Mulian's pilgrimage to string together many stories. Except for "Little Nun Going Down the Mountain," it is completely different from the carved "Mulian Saves His Mother." One section, "Wu Song Fights the Tiger," is played by two people, A and B, one strong and one weak. First, A plays Wu Song and B plays the tiger, and A beats B so hard that B complains. A says, "You are the tiger, if I don't beat you, won't you bite me to death!" B has to ask to switch roles, but is bitten so badly by A that he complains again. A says, "You are Wu Song, if I don't bite you, won't you beat me to death?" I think this is in no way inferior to the fables of Aesop of Greece or Sologub of Russia.

If we collect such works all over the country, there will probably be many more. But naturally, there are shortcomings. It has always been blocked by difficult characters and difficult articles, and isolated from modern trends of thought. Therefore, if Chinese culture is to move upwards together, we must promote mass language, mass writing, and even more so, the Latinization of writing.

Younger Brother (10) 255

— Zhou Wen

Once, I saw in the newspaper that the war had started again. It seemed very fierce, and representatives of seven or eight large armies were busy. This one ran over, that one ran over. Then there were telegrams. This one wanted to defend his homeland, and that one wanted to defend his homeland. The situation was getting tense step by step. And it was large-scale. The area where the front lines met was not far from where my younger brother was. Naturally, they would participate in the front lines again this time.

I was very worried about him. He was just a probationary officer at this time, and it would be no problem to send him to the front lines. He used to send a letter once a week, but after a month, he didn't send any more. I was very anxious and wrote to ask the family, and the family also wrote to ask me. Maybe he's dead this time. The newspaper once published such a message, saying that in this war, many foreigners took telescopes and watched the battle on high mountains, seeing the two armies fighting hand-to-hand, with tens of thousands of casualties, and thought that even the First World War was no more than this. Ah, it's over! I sadly threw the newspaper aside, looking at the gray sky outside the window, and I regretted that I hadn't persuaded my younger brother to go home earlier!

Supplement to the Shanghai Shen Bao

Talking Points

After the Invention of Machines 256

— Xing An

The civilization of the twentieth century is the civilization of machines. Since the invention of machines in the nineteenth century, human society has undergone a drastic change. This change has determined the fate of modern humans. After the invention of machines, what kind of impact did they have on human society? This varies depending on people's different perspectives.

Some people say that after the invention of machines, the productive forces of society suddenly increased hundreds of times. In the era of handicrafts, the production methods were extremely crude, relying only on human hands and crude tools to manufacture goods, so the productive forces were very weak. The machine industry era was much more advanced. After the production methods were improved, one machine was enough to replace the work of hundreds or thousands of people, so the productive forces increased day by day. As productive forces increased, humanity's material desires were fully satisfied. Moreover, along with the increase in productive forces, the material construction of society naturally progressed. Before the nineteenth century, had the world ever seen a huge ship like the modern one that traverses the vast ocean? Had it ever seen an electrical engineering project like the modern one that can supply the needs of all residents of a large city? These material constructions are precisely the gifts of the invention of machines.

However, another group of people say that after the invention of machines, a clear phenomenon that appears before our eyes in society is the vast gap between the rich and poor classes of humanity. After the invention of machines, although the productive forces of society have increased greatly, this increase is only the happiness of a few who own machines, while the majority of laborers have fallen into an extremely miserable situation. Here there is a distinction between the bourgeoisie and the working class that did not exist before the nineteenth century. The existence of this kind of class is the evil produced after the invention of machines. In addition, the second bad fact after the invention of machines is the mechanization of human work. Work is sacred, but it must have some interest. Before the invention of machines, human work was mostly based on one's own abilities and interests, so the work was somewhat artistic. However, after machines were invented, the working situation changed. Countless workers work in factories. On the surface, it seems that the workers are driving the machines, but in reality, the machines are using the workers. Workers have simply become slaves to the machines. The dryness and monotony of this kind of work can be imagined.

The above two statements each have their own partial reasons. But the great contribution that machines have made to our human society is a clear fact that no one can deny. And the various bad pathological conditions that have arisen are innumerable. However, in our observation, the invention of machines cannot but be said to be the infinite happiness of mankind. Because we have machines, we can use their power to improve our human lives and raise our human culture. As for the bad influences that they have left us, as long as we humans are good at using and adjusting them, and can use them well in beneficial aspects, the bad parts are not difficult to eliminate immediately. Otherwise, the machine itself has no toxicity. The various evils presented by modern human society due to the invention of machines are all expressions of human's own sins.

A Memory of Boating on the Liwa Lita River 257

— Wen Bing

It's a past event, originally a very interesting subject matter, I don't know why it has been delayed until today that I pick up my pen to write a "recollection." My personality is a bit "indolent," and even writing has been infected, which should be very dangerous. I have this self-awareness.

Liwa Lita is a famous place in Shanghai. That day, I went swimming with some friends in the afternoon, and we agreed to go boating again in the evening. At eight or nine o'clock in the evening, a bright moon hung outside the eastern horizon, and the milky white light shone through the sleeping universe, exceptionally serene and exceptionally comfortable. We were sitting in a group on the school's lawn, talking about everything. Tong, like a monkey, jumped and shouted nearby, saying that the boat was ready, and Nan Gong had already paddled a few rounds. In fact, saying it was ready was not as accurate as saying it had been stolen, the boat was from the school, and it was always locked up and not open to the public. Tong had a key that happened to fit, so he had the exclusive right to boat every night. When we got to the riverbank, we found that Ru had dropped out. Ju said he was preparing snacks, and we were relieved that he wasn't "missing."

We stole two boats. The cabins were narrow. It seemed that the boat builders had only intended them for lovers to paddle. It was indeed a bit crowded for three people to sit, and as soon as we sat on them, the boats seemed to sink, and the draft was particularly deep. So a problem arose. There was "Luo," whose weight was always over 300 pounds. There were six of us in total, and each boat was supposed to have three people, which was fair and selfless, but only he was difficult to allocate. After pushing and pulling for a while, Ru finally pulled him onto his boat.

Originally, everyone was in high spirits. It was late at night, and the weather was particularly cool and comfortable. The two boats raced for a few laps. When everyone reached the point where their strength was exhausted, they propped up the punts and stopped in the middle of the water. This was when Ru showed off his merits. He put the prepared soda and snacks on the bow of the boat. This was completely a practice of communism, no, it was simply directing a looting behavior, and they were snatched away in a flash. However, there is something to be praised, which is that although it was looting, it was still evenly distributed. The six mouths stopped at the same time. The so-called looting was actually just a different word for "playing around."

The time was unusually quiet, and the people were unusually happy. We sipped soda and chewed on candy. All the past frustrations and sorrows that everyone had disappeared like lightning. The endless discussions and endless laughter made us seem like six natural darlings, all living in paradise.

Just as we were chewing happily and talking forgetfully, two boats of the same size suddenly paddled over from the right. They were two pairs of lovers, the rustling sound of oars echoing the continuous singing, drawing our attention. Everyone couldn't help but feel sentimental. We were all too pitiful and too distressed. If only... it would be a scene to envy.

So we mustered our strength again, re-rocked our oars, endured the watery shadows of the moon, and paddled to the dark end of the river. Ah, there were more secrets here. Countless boats were quietly propped up on the bank. Some were snuggling and sleeping in the cabin, and some were on the shore, squatting and whispering. Suddenly a burst of nervous lewd laughter came from the shadows. This environment made us unbearable, and we agreed to row back to the other side of the river. Before long, we rowed to Liwa Lita Village. This is a scenic spot, an elegant scene. On the shore is a huge paradise, with dance floors, cafes, the reflection of neon lights, and the noisy sound of jazz music. Kun listened ecstatically, his eyes still wide open. I deliberately turned the boat left and right, scaring him to the point of trembling, and he begged me for mercy. In a flash, Tong and the others' boat had disappeared. It turned out that they could no longer resist the temptation of this environment and had rowed to the dock to go ashore. We had no choice but to row back quickly. At this time, there was no sound, and the silence was so profound that it seemed like there were small insects jumping and chirping in the grass on the shore.

This night's outing, although it dispelled a lot of pent-up feelings, also suffered endless annoyance, especially afterwards the body felt particularly tired. Lying on Ju's bed, I slept until noon the next day, still unable to get out of bed like a lazy snake.

Singing for the Sun 258

— Xi Zhen

("The bottom nature of human beings is to experience the sun,

Our deep and heavy temperament should not be against the sun." 丨丨 D·HJ· Lawrence: "Birds, Beasts and Flowers")

Let's just say that the arena of life should be like purgatory, that's fine: Looking at the sea of future days, what undulates in between is hunger, shame, suffering, adversity: For many years, using one eye to look at the movement of social history, but also having to keep one eye on taking care of one's own survival. There are no red cherries and yellow pineapples in the mixed wine of human life, we know this best, but we keep drinking it.

Let's say that life is like purgatory, but there is also a chance to see the sun in purgatory. In the morning, isn't it? The sun is big, red, like a cartwheel sunflower, releasing many needles. People look at it, and their eyes are scorched: but it is hot, healthy, hardworking, and powerful, this light, eliminating the darkness of the night, blackening the pale skin of the young masters and ladies. Filling the wheat ears of autumn, seeping into the curtains of the hospital ward, accompanying the wanderings of the lonely.

But, if the arena of life is really like purgatory, then that is something to be thankful for. Really, purgatory is heaven for us. Isn't it? Even in purgatory, you can see the sun; but we live on the underground floor, and for people living on the underground floor, the sun exists forever only in the fiction of dreams.

People living on the underground floor have no memories, no planning, no sadness, and no suspicion. Of course, the memories of the past and the planning for the future have simply become a kind of decoration for us. We have no right to want these things. At first, we can't want them, but, you know, after getting used to the darkness, we simply disdain them. All we know is "now", "now" is real, bloody, but we have to grasp it, grab it desperately, not letting it slip away; otherwise, we would have long lost the possibility of survival. Just like the old miners who work in the underground floor of the mine day and night, hammering the dead coal lumps minute by minute, they have to concentrate their attention on the present instant. If you encounter an accidental explosion, you must have the agility of a dog to immediately lie down, otherwise you will be destroyed.

Of course, no one wants to be destroyed. In this way, even if they are old, they have to grasp the flashing moment of the existing present. Who can still remember the lively chrysanthemums and laughter of their youth, and the sunshine of their childhood that once shone on them?

But people living on the underground floor know how to commemorate the sun; the sun should not be a dream, people in a previous moment may have seen his bright arm, and then it forever becomes an indelible memory. And at present, in the dark crowd, the sun is talked about like a myth.

Remembering, remembering; no, even striving to search for it, but what's the use? The sun and we are isolated, isolated by the thick curtain woven by the heavy whips of life.

It is surprising that the sun of the twentieth century has also been commodified; "Upper-class people" play tennis, swim, and perform gilded love comedies under the sun; that sun is also hot, charming, of the southern orchards.

And these are not for the people living on the underground floor, we don't have them.

But it is not that we who live on the underground floor are inherently without them. We got them and then were isolated from them. How difficult it is for people to try to tear away this layer of life's curtain. However, for the sake of the sun, we can endure anything.

People without the sun cannot live, so their children are without the sun? Who says that? That's right, even if they live on the underground floor, the sun still exists in their memories, forever, forever.

Even if it's just in memory, I have my sun, and only my sun can make me live.
